<div id="review_3529642787" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3529642787" />
    <a title="Barack Liu" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/112166097-barack-liu"><img alt="Barack Liu" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587600519p2/112166097.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3529642787?book_show_action=true">Sep 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Barack Liu" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Barack Liu" href="/user/show/112166097-barack-liu">Barack Liu</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3529642787" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9768241149739587665"> <br/>178-The Wisdom of Life-Arthur Schopenhauer-Phylosophy-1851<br/>Barack<br/>2018/07/15<br/>2020/06/11<br/><br/> <br/>—— " Life swings between two extremes: pain and boredom. The nature of happiness is negative, and the nature of pain is affirmative. Happiness does not come from happiness, but from the absence of pain. If there is neither pain nor boredom, That is the greatest happiness in life. "<br/> <br/>"The Wisdom of Life" comes from "Appendices and Supplements", which was first published in Germany in 1851. It explores the princip</span>
  <span id="freeText9768241149739587665" style="display:none"> <br />178-The Wisdom of Life-Arthur Schopenhauer-Phylosophy-1851<br />Barack<br />2018/07/15<br />2020/06/11<br /><br /> <br />—— " Life swings between two extremes: pain and boredom. The nature of happiness is negative, and the nature of pain is affirmative. Happiness does not come from happiness, but from the absence of pain. If there is neither pain nor boredom, That is the greatest happiness in life. "<br /> <br />"The Wisdom of Life" comes from "Appendices and Supplements", which was first published in Germany in 1851. It explores the principles that life should follow from a secular perspective with "elegant style".<br /> <br />Schopenhauer was born in Danzig, Germany (now Gdansk, Poland) in 1788 and died in 1860. His father is a successful businessman and his mother is a well-known writer. He studied at Göttingen University. He was the first person in the history of philosophy to openly oppose rationalist philosophy and pioneered irrational philosophy. He was also one of the founders and main representatives of voluntarism, and believed that the will to life is the power that governs the operation of the world. Representative works: "The World as Will and Appearance", "The Wisdom of Life", "Appendices and Supplements", etc.<br /> <br />Part of the catalog<br />1. Basic division<br />2. Man's self<br />3. Property owned by people<br />4. The appearance of people<br />5. Advice and motto<br />6. All stages of life<br /> <br />Everyone has three attributes: the person himself, the things outside the person, and the way the person shows to others. Oneself does not depend on others to exist, wisdom, appearance, view of the world, etc.; things outside the body depend on others to exist, wealth, status, family, friends, etc.; the appearance shown to others changes due to the situation, children, students, citizens , Parents, etc.<br /> <br />Happiness depends largely on ourselves. This view may be somewhat subjective or idealistic, but external objectivity often affects our view of the world by indirectly affecting ourselves. The world is a mirror. Even when experiencing the same thing, some people find it interesting and some people feel extremely bored. This difference is caused by the difference in the inner spiritual world.<br /> <br />It is said that when Socrates saw the luxury goods sold in the market, he said: "I don't need a lot of things." Apart from basic material needs, people with rich spiritual world usually have their own happiness. Less affected by the external world.<br /> <br />In order to achieve happiness, health is the first priority, because it is internal, so it overwhelms all external benefits. After reaching this point, a person should pursue as much as possible a position, occupation and lifestyle that matches his personality. The tragedies caused by this mismatch are numerous. Life swings between two extremes, painful and boring. Health avoids pain, and work consistent with personality avoids boredom.<br /> <br />"To enjoy yourself" has a deep meaning, because it implies that happiness comes from oneself. Pain and boredom are the deadly enemies of life. The lower class struggles with pain for life, while the upper class struggles with boredom. When the inner is empty, one seeks to get attention from the outside. But the rich spiritual world often increases the intensity of emotion. In my opinion, extreme coldness or ruthlessness may also be a strong emotion.<br /> <br />Schopenhauer made a rather arbitrary judgment: either vulgar or lonely. But its essence is worth learning. Leisure is the essence of life. When you want to understand a person, you might as well see how he spends his leisure time. Smoking and playing cards are very popular pastimes that replace thinking. They are a bit like a person's unconscious knuckle tapping on the table when he is bored.<br /> <br />For the spiritually rich, real life is more a means than an end. In addition to their material life, they often live an ideological life. In healthy after Kang achieve, a strong happiness is the ability to explore, training and play to their talents, and a strong Unfortunately, the above process is thwarted not be completed.<br /> <br />For those who lack spiritual pursuit, the greatest happiness comes from the senses. Almost all sensory pleasures are short-lived. For this reason, the constant pursuit of sensory enjoyment again and again has become the biggest goal of survival. Extreme examples are often easy to see the essence of things, and drugs are an extreme example.<br /> <br />Zhuangzi said in "Xiaoyaoyou", it is universally praised without persuasion, and the world is not without discouragement. Most people's views of us are actually not important. These views are worth considering only when they indirectly or directly affect our real life. Reducing our sensitivity to the opinions of others is a suggestion given by Schopenhauer, but it is more or less self-conscious.<br /> <br />The seclusion life is alluring because it saves us from living in the sight of others, thus making our hearts peaceful. And can the lower classes, who make up the vast majority of the population, enjoy the joy of life? Generally speaking, it is more difficult. On the one hand, material deprivation will cause external pain, and on the other hand, spiritual deprivation will make it difficult for people to feel the joy of being alone and inner peace.<br /> <br />The production of pleasure is the elimination of intentional inhibition, so each sensory pleasure can only last for a relatively short time. The maximum number of transport a person can get, life is lived a lifetime but did not bear the pain on any great mental or physical, and not once felt very strongly pleasure. Strong pleasure is often short-lived, it will make people indulge in her charm, and thus bear the great pain that comes with it.<br /> <br />In the rich spiritual world, knowing oneself is a permanent motif that continues every day until the death. To know yourself, you need to recognize your primary needs and true wishes. Generally speaking, this kind of willingness will become more and more vague as we age, because we have more and more pursued, and thus become less and less sure of the importance of each possession and pursuit.<br /> <br />The pursuit of happiness comes from nature, and almost everyone knows it. Avoiding pain means fighting against instinct all the time. Just like Sisyphus in Greek mythology, he must always fight against the gravity of the boulder. Kant said in "Principles of Moral Metaphysics" that the so-called freedom is not to do whatever one wants, but to dominate oneself. So being limited to moderation helps to avoid pain and increase happiness.<br /> <br />In "Mencius", there is a story. During the Spring and Autumn and Warring States period, a certain monarch asked a certain doctor to visit the people to ask about talents. The doctor looked for three years and finally recommended a man to the monarch. The monarch expected to ask the person what special talents he had, and the doctor replied, no. The monarch was disappointed, the doctor explained, but he did not have the shortcomings of most people. The monarch then reused the person.<br /> <br />Before going to bed every night, you might as well check your actions during the day one by one and be diligent in reflection. At the same time, regular diaries and records of special events are also helpful for happiness. Too much frustration about the past and what has been lost, as well as the excess expectations for the future and what has not been achieved, make people often ignore the present and what they have.<br /> <br />Schopenhauer regarded every sleep and early rise as a death and resurrection. The discomfort of getting up is similar to the difficulty of birth, and the delay of going to bed is regarded as the reluctance to die. The morning is like a young man, the afternoon is like a middle-aged person, and the evening is like the end of life.<br /> <br />" Happiness is not an easy thing: it is difficult for her to ask for it, but it is impossible for her to get it elsewhere. ——Chambert . "<br /> <br />Our emphasis on the importance of consciousness does not mean that we deny the meaning of matter . In fact, matter is the basis of consciousness, but it is nothing more than matter . Matter itself is not an end . Matter is not the decisive factor in our happiness. Happiness is a feeling. It is indeed affected by matter, but in the end it depends on our own inner thoughts.<br /> <br />" Such a "happy survival", from a purely objective examination, or more precisely, through calm and careful thinking (because subjective judgment is involved here), can be defined as definitely better than non-survival. Since "happy survival" "It is such a definition, then we can say this: We are attached to this existence because of this existence itself, not because of the fear of death; and we long to see that this existence can last forever . "<br /> <br />" Generally speaking, the wise men of all ages have spoken the same words, and fools-that is, the innumerable majority of people in all ages-have done exactly the opposite and the same thing. Therefore, Voltaire said Past: "When we leave this world, this world is still stupid and evil, no different from what we discovered when we first came into this world. " "<br /> <br />" I think the fundamental difference that determines the fate of a mortal lies in three contents. They are: 1) The person's self, that is, what belongs to a person's personality in the broadest sense. Therefore, it includes a person's health, strength, appearance, temperament, Moral character, spiritual intelligence and its potential development. 2) The things outside the body that a person owns, that is, property and other possessions. 3) The way a person shows to others, which can be understood as: what a person presents in the eyes of others Appearance, that is, what people think of him. The opinions of others can be divided into reputation, status, and reputation. "<br /> <br />" The first disciple of Epicurus, Mencedoros, once titled one of his chapters in his writings with the title: "The reason for our happiness lies within ourselves, not outside ourselves. . "Indeed, for a person's happiness, even for his whole way of living, this is obviously the most important person from the body of the inner qualities that will determine whether the person can get inner happiness, because happiness or whether the human heart Inner pain is firstly the product of human feelings, desires and thoughts. All things outside of human beings only indirectly affect human happiness.<br /> <br />Therefore, the same external things and the same circumstances have different effects on each of us; everyone in the same environment lives in a different world. Because directly related to a person is the person's views on things, his feelings, and his intentions. External things can only play a role when they stimulate him. What kind of world each person lives in, first of all depends on the person's understanding of this world. This world is different because of the differences in the mind and spirit of each person. Therefore, each person's world is barren, shallow and superficial, or colorful, interesting and full of meaning-it depends on each person's mind. "<br /> <br />I think that the most essential difference between people and people is the difference in how they look at problems. In other words , when different people have the same objective conditions, they will react differently. These reactions reflect the fundamental differences among people . Of course , some people are born with wealth, status , beauty , and health. Even if they don't manage their lives so carefully , they may still be more fortunate than those who are born poor, humble, ugly , and weak .<br /> <br />But since this is something we cannot change, then we should not discuss it too much, but should focus on what we can change. Just like an excellent chess player, he is not good because he can get a good deck every time , but because he can make full use of the advantages of good cards when he gets good cards. And when he gets a bad hand, he can also fully avoid the disadvantage of a bad hand.<br /> <br />" Real life, that is, every moment of the current experience, is composed of two parts: the subject and the object-although the subject and the object are closely related to each other and are indispensable, just like the oxygen and hydrogen that together constitute water. Face it When the objects are exactly the same, different subjects mean that the reality constituted is completely different, and vice versa. It can be seen that the combination of the most beautiful and best object and the dull and inferior subject can only produce inferior reality. It's like watching beautiful scenery under bad weather, or shooting these scenery with a badly blurred camera.<br /> <br />Or, let's put it in a more simple language: just as everyone is confined to their own skin, everyone is also confined to their own consciousness. One can only live directly in one's own consciousness. Therefore, the external world does not help him much. On the stage, actors play various roles: servants, soldiers, or princes and generals. However, the difference between these characters is only external and furry, and the inner core under these superficial phenomena is the same; they are nothing more than pitiful, painful and troublesome actors.<br /> <br />The situation is the same in real life. The different status and wealth possessed by each person endows the individual with different roles, but the inner happiness of each person will not be different due to the different outer roles. On the contrary, these people are also poor creatures full of pain and trouble. The specific content of worries and worries varies from person to person; but their form, that is, their essence, is similar; the degree of pain and anxiety will vary, but these differences do not match the differences in people's status and wealth. That is, it does not match the role played by everyone.<br /> <br />For humans, everything that exists and happens always exists and happens directly in his consciousness. Therefore, it is obvious that the composition of human consciousness is the primary key. In most cases, the subject consciousness is more important than the objects and forms presented in consciousness. All beautiful and interesting things, reflected by a fool's sluggish consciousness, will become dull and boring. "<br /> <br />" The extent to which our happiness depends on ourselves, that is, on our personality. But in most cases, we only consider luck, consider possessions, or consider how we look in the eyes of others. In fact, , Luck will get better, and even if we are rich inside, we won’t have too much demand for luck. In contrast, a dull-headed person will be dull-headed throughout his life, and a fool will die. He is still an idiot, even if he is in heaven, surrounded by heavenly beauties. Therefore, Goethe said: The public, regardless of high or low, always admit that the greatest fortune that all beings can get is their own personality. "<br /> <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9768241149739587665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cXkgvQtJ89RXFPR41Rm0DuDJaoc/GtOm4Jl3dBk0g7t8JkQ/i+Qtoe4OsK0pZ5Twn5rejEiMVRoPs6N8/dttVQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('8pc37w9a8yll7YBLgUeATj2lptswTKhJqnWlJmKYgLv/yFNtj/ctXNz3xJ59OaCwQvYS0EfaLvVFX3EuhnduVQ==')})
  }

Nietzsche s influe<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3347002747193434058\" style=\"display:none\">Friedrich Wilhelm Nietzsche (1844-1900) was a German philosopher. His writing included critiques of religion, morality, contemporary culture, philosophy and science, using a distinctive style and displaying a fondness for aphorism. Nietzsche s influence remains substantial within and beyond philosophy, notably in existentialism and postmodernism. He began his career as a philologist before turning to philosophy. At the age of 24 he became Professor of Classical Philology at the University of Basel, but resigned in 1879 due to health problems, which would plague him for most of his life. In 1889 he exhibited symptoms of serious mental illness, living out his remaining years in the care of his mother and sister until his death in 1900. His works include From my Life (1858), On Music (1858), Napoleon III as a President (1862), Free Willand Fate (1862), My Life (1864), The Birth of Tragedy (1872), Richard Wagner in Bayreuth (1876), Human, All-Too-Human (1878), Beyond Good and Evil (1886), The Antichrist (1888) and Ecce Homo (1888).<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"3347002747193434058\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));;       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/11682.Arthur_Schopenhauer">About Arthur Schopenhauer</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7760460504888951935">Arthur Schopenhauer was born in the city of Danzig (then part of the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth; present day Gdańsk, Poland) and was a German philosopher best known for his work <i>The World as Will and Representation</i>. Schopenhauer attempted to make his career as an academic by correcting and expanding Immanuel Kant's philosophy concerning the way in which we experience the world.<br/><br/>He was the son o</span>
  <span id="freeText7760460504888951935" style="display:none">Arthur Schopenhauer was born in the city of Danzig (then part of the Polish–Lithuanian Commonwealth; present day Gdańsk, Poland) and was a German philosopher best known for his work <i>The World as Will and Representation</i>. Schopenhauer attempted to make his career as an academic by correcting and expanding Immanuel Kant's philosophy concerning the way in which we experience the world.<br /><br />He was the son of author <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/821551.Johanna_Schopenhauer" title="Johanna Schopenhauer" rel="nofollow noopener">Johanna Schopenhauer</a> and the older brother of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/4554434.Adele_Schopenhauer" title="Adele Schopenhauer" rel="nofollow noopener">Adele Schopenhauer</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7760460504888951935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
